href=\"/story/news/nation/2017/03/07/wikileaks-says-has-published-cia-hacking-codes/98844256/\">the release of CIA documents by WikiLeaks</a> on Tuesday.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>While Trump praised the organization during the 2016 presidential campaign, he has been at odds with them in recent months, including over <a href=\"https://twitter.com/wikileaks/status/824604277003976704?lang=en\">Trump's attack on Wikileaks source Chelsea Manning</a> and <a href=\"https://twitter.com/wikileaks/status/823212055322853382?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">the president's ongoing refusal to release his tax returns</a>. Trump last\u00a0mentioned WikiLeaks on Twitter on\u00a0Nov. 5, 2016, three days prior to Election Day, when<a href=\"https://twitter.com/realDonaldTrump/status/795017781423067136\"> he posted a story</a> about a WikiLeaks release and Clinton campaign aides.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>Here are some of the notable times Trump has talked about WikiLeaks in the past:</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><h2 class=\"presto-h2\">Dec. 2, 2010</h2><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p><strong>Trump:</strong> \"I think it's disgraceful.\"</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p><strong>Where:</strong> In a preview for a December 2010 interview with\u00a0Kilmeade &amp; Friends, <a href=\"http://www.cnn.com/2017/01/04/politics/kfile-trump-wikileaks/\">as reported by CNN</a></p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p><strong>Context:</strong> Trump, years prior to announcing his presidential campaign, appeared on the Kilmeade &amp; Friends, a radio show on Fox News. In a clip posted on YouTube to preview the interview, host Brian Kilmeade mentioned WikiLeaks, saying, \"You didn't have anything to do with it, did you?\" Trump replied, \"Nope, but I think it's disgraceful. I think there should be a death penalty or something.\" Earlier that week in a move that helped bring WikiLeaks into international view, the nonprofit organization began releasing leaked U.S. embassy cables.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><div id=\"module-position-PyqSEfEZsHk\" class=\"story-asset oembed-asset\"><div class=\"blog-oembed-wrap \"><div\n        class=\"js-oembed blog-oembed blog-oembed-youtube blog-oembed-type-video\"\n        data-oembed-type=\"video\"\n        data-oembed-provider=\"youtube\"><iframe width=\"480\" height=\"270\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/fDEDQFj9sFk?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen></iframe></div></div></div><!-- cxenseparse_start --><h2 class=\"presto-h2\">July 23, 2016</h2><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p><strong>Trump:</strong> Went on a tweetstorm to talk about the WikiLeaks release of emails from the Democratic National Committee. One tweet: \"Leaked e-mails of DNC show plans to destroy Bernie Sanders. Mock his heritage and much more. On-line from Wikileakes, really vicious. RIGGED\"</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p><strong>Where:</strong> Twitter</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p><strong>Context:</strong> On July 22, 2016, WikiLeaks dumped thousands of emails and attachments from top aides at the DNC. <a href=\"/story/news/politics/onpolitics/2016/07/23/dnc-wikileaks-emails-sanders-wasserman-schultz-weaver/87475070/\">The emails raised questions</a> about whether Democrats tried to undercut Sen. Bernie Sanders' presidential campaign in order to favor Hillary Clinton.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><div id=\"module-position-PyqSEfHo0CE\" class=\"story-asset oembed-asset\"><div class=\"blog-oembed-wrap \"><div\n        class=\"js-oembed blog-oembed blog-oembed-twitter blog-oembed-type-rich\"\n        data-oembed-type=\"rich\"\n        data-oembed-provider=\"twitter\"><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\"><p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">The Wikileaks e-mail release today was so bad to Sanders that it will make it impossible for him to support her, unless he is a fraud!</p>&mdash; Donald J. Trump (@realDonaldTrump) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/realDonaldTrump/status/756962332228612096\">July 23, 2016</a></blockquote></div></div></div><!-- cxenseparse_start --><h2 class=\"presto-h2\">Oct. 10, 2016</h2><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p><strong>Trump:</strong> \"I love WikiLeaks!\"</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p><strong>Where:</strong> A campaign rally in Pennsylvania</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p><strong>Context:</strong> A few days before then-candidate Donald Trump spoke to supporters in Wilkes-Barre, Pa., WikiLeaks began releasing the emails of Hillary Clinton campaign chairman John Podesta.\u00a0The emails were dropped <a href=\"/story/news/politics/onpolitics/2016/10/07/trump-washington-post-women-billy-bush-video/91743992/\">within an hour</a> of the release of the now infamous <em>Access Hollywood</em>\u00a0video of Trump bragging of kissing and groping women (and using some choice language to do so). At his campaign rally, Trump read the excerpts of Clinton's past closed-door speeches, which were contained within the emails released by WikiLeaks (and <a href=\"/story/news/politics/elections/2016/10/12/fact-check-trump-clinton-wikileaks/91967506/\">he twisted some of those excerpts while doing so</a>).</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><div id=\"module-position-PyqSEfGrfkU\" class=\"story-asset oembed-asset\"><div class=\"blog-oembed-wrap \"><div\n        class=\"js-oembed blog-oembed blog-oembed-youtube blog-oembed-type-video\"\n        data-oembed-type=\"video\"\n        data-oembed-provider=\"youtube\"><iframe width=\"480\" height=\"270\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/mUtT0b0EnSw?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen></iframe></div></div></div><!-- cxenseparse_start --><h2 class=\"presto-h2\">Feb. 16, 2017</h2><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p><strong>Trump:</strong> \"So in one case you\u2019re talking about highly classified information. In the other case you\u2019re talking about John Podesta saying bad things about the boss.\"</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p><strong>Where:</strong><a href=\"https://www.whitehouse.gov/the-press-office/2017/02/16/remarks-president-trump-press-conference\">Press conference at the White House</a></p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p><strong>Context:</strong> During the press conference, Trump addressed leaks that resulted in the resignation of National Security Adviser Michael Flynn earlier that week, saying they were\u00a0a \"real problem.\" When a reporter noted that the president had encouraged leaks during the campaign, specifically from WikiLeaks, Trump replied that those releases\u00a0did not compare because it was not classified: Podesta \"said terrible things about her. But it wasn't classified information.\"</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><div id=\"module-position-PyqSEfHFtEM\" class=\"story-asset gallery-asset\"><div class=\"card-film inactive\"></div><div "http://rssfeeds.usatoday.com/~/278644772/0/usatoday-newstopstories~How-Trump-feels-about-WikiLeaks-A-timeline/", "date": "03-08-2017", "source": "new-york-times", "text": "CLOSE Skip in Skip x Embed x Share The website claims they have several hundred million lines of code from the CIA's hacking arsenal that includes damaging information. USA TODAY NETWORK\n\nPresident Trump has remained mum about the release of CIA documents by WikiLeaks on Tuesday.\n\nWhile Trump praised the organization during the 2016 presidential campaign, he has been at odds with them in recent months, including over Trump's attack on Wikileaks source Chelsea Manning and the president's ongoing refusal to release his tax returns. Trump last mentioned WikiLeaks on Twitter on Nov. 5, 2016, three days prior to Election Day, when he posted a story about a WikiLeaks release and Clinton campaign aides.\n\nHere are some of the notable times Trump has talked about WikiLeaks in the past:\n\nDec. 2, 2010\n\nTrump: \"I think it's disgraceful.\"\n\nWhere: In a preview for a December 2010 interview with Kilmeade & Friends, as reported by CNN\n\nContext: Trump, years prior to announcing his presidential campaign, appeared on the Kilmeade & Friends, a radio show on Fox News. In a clip posted on YouTube to preview the interview, host Brian Kilmeade mentioned WikiLeaks, saying, \"You didn't have anything to do with it, did you?\" Trump replied, \"Nope, but I think it's disgraceful. I think there should be a death penalty or something.\" Earlier that week in a move that helped bring WikiLeaks into international view, the nonprofit organization began releasing leaked U.S. embassy cables.\n\nJuly 23, 2016\n\nTrump: Went on a tweetstorm to talk about the WikiLeaks release of emails from the Democratic National Committee. One tweet: \"Leaked e-mails of DNC show plans to destroy Bernie Sanders. Mock his heritage and much more. On-line from Wikileakes, really vicious. RIGGED\"\n\nWhere: Twitter\n\nContext: On July 22, 2016, WikiLeaks dumped thousands of emails and attachments from top aides at the DNC. The emails raised questions about whether Democrats tried to undercut Sen. Bernie Sanders' presidential campaign in order to favor Hillary Clinton.\n\nThe Wikileaks e-mail release today was so bad to Sanders that it will make it impossible for him to support her, unless he is a fraud! \u2014 Donald J. Trump (@realDonaldTrump) July 23, 2016\n\nOct. 10, 2016\n\nTrump: \"I love WikiLeaks!\"\n\nWhere: A campaign rally in Pennsylvania\n\nContext: A few days before then-candidate Donald Trump spoke to supporters in Wilkes-Barre, Pa., WikiLeaks began releasing the emails of Hillary Clinton campaign chairman John Podesta. The emails were dropped within an hour of the release of the now infamous Access Hollywood video of Trump bragging of kissing and groping women (and using some choice language to do so). At his campaign rally, Trump read the excerpts of Clinton's past closed-door speeches, which were contained within the emails released by WikiLeaks (and he twisted some of those excerpts while doing so).\n\nFeb. 16, 2017\n\nTrump: \"So in one case you\u2019re talking about highly classified information. In the other case you\u2019re talking about John Podesta saying bad things about the boss.\"\n\nWhere:Press conference at the White House\n\nContext: During the press conference, Trump addressed leaks that resulted in the resignation of National Security Adviser Michael Flynn earlier that week, saying they were a \"real problem.\" When a reporter noted that the president had encouraged leaks during the campaign, specifically from WikiLeaks, Trump replied that those releases did not compare because it was not classified: Podesta \"said terrible things about her. But it wasn't classified information.\"\n\nRead or Share this story: http://usat.ly/2m2IR8F", "images":
